(date of statement).Persons covered by the order.Are obliged to make the declaration, all commercial or public utility organizationsfor the purpose of providing accommodation or for the sale of foodstuffs and beverages toconsume on site, such as hotels, furnished houses, boarding houses, restaurants, drinking establishments, cafes,cafes and restaurants, shipping companies, premises of clubs and societies, establishments forsick or convalescent, houses of education, seminaries, boarding schools, etc.Are required to make the declaration, under the same conditions, all natural or civil persons,all commercial or industrial enterprises governed by private or public law, in particular also institutionstions of the communes or of the cult, which lend. rent, work or otherwise hold,intended for the establishments referred to in the 1st paragraph, the bed, household or table linen used inthe said holdings, p. ex. laundries, linen hire houses and sewing workshops.Declaration of stocks.The declaration must be made no later than December 24, 1917, by means of special bulletins and bygoods, at the «Militärisches Textilbeschaffungsamt», in Bruxelles, 13, ruo de Quatre-Arm. The bulletins are delivered, on request, by the aforesaid office, or by the \"Kroischefs\" (headsof district) or \"Abschnittskommandanturen\" competent; they must be completed in such a way as to provide aoverview of the species and quantities of declarable objects.Purchase Provisions.The “Militärisches Textilbeschaffungsamt” is authorized to purchase the goods to be declaredunder this Order; it will take as a basis the prices which, in Belgium, were normally paid inmanufacturers on July 25, 1914, increased by a maximum of 100%.When amicable purchase is not possible, the goods may be expropriated. In thiscase, a receipt will be given to the person who will issue them and the payment of the indemnity will be settled by the“Reichsentschädigungskommission” (Imperial Compensation Commission).For farms mainly used for the accommodation of German soldiers or civilians,the purchase will take place by mutual agreement with the competent local \"Kommandantur\".Use and conservation of objects.Subject to the requirements of Article 4, the provisions of this Order do not provide anyrestriction on the right to continue to use regularly, in the own exploitation of the interested parties, theobjects which must be declared, and, with regard to existing rental establishments, to continueto rent these objects.In addition, it is prohibited, in a general and absolute way, to dispose of objects, to transport themand, apart from the normal wear and tear resulting from the use authorized by the 1st paragraph, to bring aany modification.Holders are obliged to keep the objects with care and to treat them appropriately.Regular bookkeeping.Any person obliged to declare must keep, for all the objects referred to in Article 1, a book ofstore allowing at all times to see the declarable stocks of used or non-used objectsAgents of military or civil authorities are authorized to supervise the observation ofpresent prescriptions, to examine the books of trade as well as the stocks stored.Subsequent statements.The declarable objects that the holdings or persons designated in article 2 will not obtain in possessiononly after the day of the statement, then of purchase or in any other way, must be declared no later than theI of the following month, for the first time on February 1, 1918.They will be subject to the same provisions as the objects already held by the holdings on the day ofraised.Ineffectiveness of previously granted exemptions from seizure.The provisions of this decree are not modified by the fact that the objects referred to themselves orthe raw materials, semi-finished or finished products from which they come would be exempt from seizureunder previous decrees or provisions.Penal provisions.maybeAnyone who, intentionally or through negligence, violates the requirements of this decree,will be punished either by imprisonment for a maximum of two years and a fine of up to 25,000 marcs,or one of these two penalties. In addition, the confiscation of the goods constituting the object of the offensepronounced in all cases; it will prevail in cases of voluntary infringement.Are applicable, the prescriptions of the decree of June 17, 1917 concerning the extension of the provisionscriminal penalties for orders taken from an economic point of view as a result of the state of war.German courts and military commanders will hear violations of this order.The requirements of Articles 4, 5, 7, 2nd paragraph, and 9, 1st paragraph, 2nd sentence, of this decree are notnot applicable to objects for which it can be established, on the statement day, that they constitute theproperty of the \"Hispano-Dutch Committee\", or the \"National Relief and Food Committee\", nor to theobjects of which these institutions will subsequently acquire possession.Brussels, November 22, 1917.The Governor General in Belgium.',\n \"News publishedGovernments.Government.German general.Daily German News.Theater of War in the West.disputed places in our hands. Beinggiven, however, that holders have an understandable desire to receive as soon as possiblefunds to be able to continue their business, make new purchases, pay salaries, etc., I havecreated aIMPORTS TO THE GOVERNOR GENERAL IN BELGIUMwhose offices will be in Brussels, 90, rue de la Loi.This Caisse will make advances on the vouchers given in exchange for the requisitioned “Massengüter”.All holders of vouchers, of German nationality, of a country allied to Germany, or Belgian residentholders in the occupied part of the country, as well as holders belonging to neutral nations, may,without distinction, take advantage of these facilities. Advances will be granted without interest.The Caisse d\\'avances will begin its operations on April 6. We can get to knowregulations governing the Caisse\\'s relations with the public: at the head office itself, with the presidentscivil administrations in the various provinces and among the district chiefs. Beinggiven, however, that holders have an understandable desire to receive as soon as possiblefunds to be able to continue their business, make new purchases, pay salaries, etc., I havecreated aIMPORTS TO THE GOVERNOR GENERAL IN BELGIUMwhose offices will be in Brussels, 90, rue de la Loi.This Caisse will make advances on the vouchers given in exchange for the requisitioned “Massengüter”.All holders of vouchers, of German nationality, of a country allied to Germany, or Belgian residentholders in the occupied part of the country, as well as holders belonging to neutral nations, may,without distinction, take advantage of these facilities. Advances will be granted without interest.The Caisse d\\'avances will begin its operations on April 6. We can get to knowregulations governing the Caisse\\'s relations with the public: at the head office itself, with the presidentscivil administrations in the various provinces and among the district chiefs. In addition, theywill be communicated to the principal banks and bankers of the occupied Belgian territory.The advances granted by the Caisse d\\'avances shall in no way delay the final paymentvouchers issued for Massengüter\" requisitioned, as envisaged in my opinion of theJanuary 9, 1915. V.S.), located in Brussels and reporting to the Head ofcivil administration to the Governor General.This Supply Office [K. V.S.] is responsible for ensuringthe distribution of potatoes intended for foodBelgian people. To this end, he has the right to also pay the consumption.potato production.In municipalities where potato stocks are insufficientto provide food for the population, the communal administrationend must, through the competent civil commissioner, declarethe missing quantity at the Supply Office,In order to meet declared needs (art. 3), the Supply Officecan determine the quantities of potatoes to be suppliedby the producing regions. The supply of these quantities is the responsibilityto the municipalities of these regions. The mayor will set the quantitiesdelivered by each producer.If a producer refuses to deliver, the head of the borough mayorder that the potatoes be expropriated, if necessaryresorting to armed force, and purchased at a price less than20 percent at the maximum prevailing price, and that ownership of suchpotatoes be allocated to such a municipality or to such a personnamed in the order. By the latter, the owner will berequired to hold ready, within a specified time, the quantity to beexpropriated. If the owner does not comply with this injunction, theborough head may assign another person to do thenecessary, at the expense of the recalcitrant owner.In determining the quantities to be expropriated, it will betaking into account the needs of the producer, in such a way that the provisionsnecessary to maintain its operation and, in particular, thoseessential to the cultivation of his land remain assured to him.If the Head of Civil Administration regulates the supply ofcertain communes without having recourse to the intermediary of the “Bureau d’appro-viewing in potatoes” (art. 10), the refusal to deliver fallsalso under the application of this article.All municipal administrations must take the necessary measuresnecessary to supply the population with potatoes,Above all, they have to make sure that there are potatoes insufficient quantities to feed the population.The municipal administrations must set, in accordance with theprovisions of the decree of September 28, 1915 (Official Bulletin of Laws andarrested p. 1090) the selling price of the potatoes purchased by themand that they will resell either directly or through theThe communal administrations have the right to occupy, in theirterritory, premises to deposit their stocks of potatoes.In the absence of an amicable agreement, the indemnity to be paid under this head to thefees will be set by the head of the district.The municipalities have the right to buy the stocks of potatoesbeing in the possession of the merchants at the time of the transaction; THEprices will have to be established according to the decree of September 28, 1915.case of refusal, art. 5, appropriated accordingly, shall apply.The Head of Civil Administration is responsible for the execution of thisstopped. It has, among other things, the right to make regulatory provisionsboth the quality of the potatoes to be delivered, the admission and paymenttion of shippers and the transport of potatoes. he canalso regulate the supply of certain municipalities without resorting tothrough the “Potato Supply Office”;in addition, he is authorized to take all other necessary measureswith a view to ensuring the supply of potatoes as it isprovided for by this order.All disputes arising from the delivery of potatoes(order of September 28, 1915 [Official Bulletin of Laws and Ordersp. 1090] and this decree) will be decided by an arbitration tribunalwho alone will be competent; at the request of one of the interested parties, this courtwill bring together through the care of the \"Potato Supply Officeterre ».Each of the interested parties must appoint an arbitrator from among the personsthat the Supply Office will choose for this purpose, or will have to invitethe Supply Office to appoint an arbitrator itself.The appointed arbitrators, as soon as they have been appointed, must meet,ascertain the facts and, if they agree on the judgment to be pronounced,they must immediately communicate to each of the interested parties thearbitration decision, which, if necessary, will indicate in figures the least-value determined by the arbitration tribunal. If the referees cannotfail to agree on the decision to be taken, the Approval Officeviewing will appoint a third arbitrator who alone will decide, howeverby adopting the viewpoint of one of the first two referees.The arbitration tribunal has the right to hear experts andwitnessesArticles 1005-1028 of the Belgian Civil Procedure Code are notapplicable to this arbitration tribunal.The arbitration tribunal decides freely who bears the costs ofits proceedings, including the costs of the parties. Compensation to be receivedby arbitrators and experts as well as those due to witnesses forloss of time and travel expenses will be determined by the Supply Office.sing.The decisions of the arbitration tribunal are without appeal.In the event of a dispute between the municipality which must deliver and the one which mustreceive the potatoes, the request for arbitration shall, as far aspossible, be made within 48 hours of the arrival of the potatoes:if necessary, this request should be made by telegram.Contraventions of the prescriptions enacted under article 10will be punished with a police or correctional prison sentenceup to one year or a fine of up to 10,000 marcs.The two penalties may be combined. When stocks are inwarehouses, depots or other places of conservation belonging to others and that the person having the right to dispose of these stocksdoes not hold them under lock and key, the owners of the said premises are responsible for observing the order.The declaration is also required from state, religious and municipal holdings. In this case, it is the responsibility of the directorscurrent operations; where operations are run by German military or civil authorities or their officialsmanagers and employees, it is up to these authorities, officials or employees to make the declaration.Are exempted from the obligation to declare, the exploitations of the Military general direction of the railroads (Militär-General-Directorate of Railways) et de l'Administration allemande des postes et des télégraphes (German Post and TelegraphThe communal administrations are responsible for the declaration with regard to buildings, factories, etc. abandonedby their owners or inhabitants or unoccupied. The local “Kommandanturen” are authorized to give municipalitiesfurther instructions on this subject.All objects which must be declared after the $ 2, are seized under this order.They can only be sold to the “Zentral-Einkaufsgesellschaft für Belgien m. b. H.” in Brussels.Any other legal provision on the objects falling under the application of the decree is prohibited, just as it is forbidden toto change ownership, to work on them or to make any modification to them, except that one can continue temporarilyto use the objects in use on a regular basis.Persons, authorities, companies, etc. referred to in § 3, are responsible for the proper preservation of the objects falling under thecation of this order. It is forbidden to hide these objects with a view to making them part of the application of the decree.In special cases, the Trade and Industry Section (Abteilung für Handel und Gewerbe) is authorized to consentother exceptions to the defense formulated in & 3, if the request is made to him in writing.Abduction by force.If the objects falling under the application of this decree are not declared (8 5), dismantled or delivered (8 6), or if they are notin time, it may be proceeded, in favor of the German Military Administration (Deutsche Heeresverwaltung), at the expense of thepossessor, to dismantling by constraint and to removal by constraint, without prejudice to the legal proceedings provided for in $ 10.For this purpose, home searches may be carried out.In the event of dismantling and forced removal, no compensation is granted.Regulations.The Head of the Civil Administration (Verwaltungschef) attached to the Governor General, Trade and Industry Section, is authorizedto publish general or special regulatory provisions concerning this Order, as well as with regard to thedismantling and delivery of objects falling under the application of this order; it may in particular, with a view to the application of the decree,prescribe operational changes in the industry, for example the merger of designated operations to $2.Penal provisions.Will be punished either by imprisonment for a maximum of 5 years and a fine of up to 50,000 marcs, or by one of these twopenalties to the exclusion of the other, whoever, intentionally or by gross negligence, will have violated the prescriptions of thisdecree or the regulatory provisions, additional instructions or other decrees to which it will give rise. will be punished witheven, anyone who has engaged or incited third parties to violate this decree or the subsequent prescriptions relating thereto, unlesshigher penalties are provided for in general criminal laws. Building domes, roofs, gutters, drains and balustrades.(23)(22)(24)Delivery Arrangements.The delivery of objects of categories i to 18 of article 2 must be done by municipalities and by districtsin accordance with the instructions given below.In the localities where the interested parties will receive a special notice inviting them to deliver, the fact of not havingreceived such notice would not exempt from the obligation to deliver. The crew was saved: The crew was saved.The General Government in Belgium',\n '1033',\n 'Governments.Government.News publishedby the governmentGerman general.Of morningLe Matin de Paris written on the date ofHow do you get rid of a journalistannoying.How do you get rid of a journalistannoying.“The regime of terror that German ferocity has been reigning for almost nine months over the evil-happy Belgium has just made a new victim in the person of a newspaper editor of theprovince of Luxemburg. This is Mr. Josen, a Belgian journalist of great merit and who had played,until the time of the war, a great political role in this province.As soon as Belgium was occupied, Mr. Josen was put by the German military authorities on the listsuspects who had to be closely watched. But he was on his guard, because he knew that theleast pretext would be enough for the Germans to arrest him, accuse him of espionage and make him suffer the fate ofso many of his unfortunate compatriots who lost their lives under the Prussian bullets.Weeks and months passed. In vain the Germans waited for an opportunity to \"make theirbusiness\" to this courageous, but prudent and circumspect man, the occasion did not come. So they decidedto proceed with one of those cowardly and infamous blows which they alone possess the mastery of.A month ago Mr. Josen intending to go to Holland went to Arlon and presented himself at the officeof the captain, head of the Kommandantur, to obtain a passport.The Hauptmann receives Mr. Josen very politely and, after examining his papers, declares himself ready for himissue the requested passport. But suddenly he gets up and says:Excuse me for a moment, I have an order to give outside, I\\'ll be right over to you.He leaves leaving Mr. Josen alone in his office. He leaves barely two minutes, comes back, settles in fronthis table and signs the visitor\\'s passport.But where is the stamp of the Kommandantur? he cries abruptly, and he begins to rummage inthe papers piled up in front of him.The stamp is not there! he howls! you stole it!And he throws himself on Mr. Josen, calls two gendarmes who run up. The prisoner is searched, holdingthe arms and — of course! - we find the stamp or rather one of the gendarmes \"removed\" it from one of the pocketsexteriors of the unfortunate Belgian journalist.This one may shout, protest, useless! He was arrested and taken, handcuffed, to Arlon prison.At the same time, the order is given to search Mr. Josen\\'s home. And then we find out howonly the Germans know how to find out - a secret cipher; we also \"discover\" the draft of a telegramencrypted which is immediately decrypted using this key, and which contains important military news,addressed to the commanders of the allied armies!That\\'s it! Mr. Josen, sent only a few days after his arrest before the council ofGerman war, is condemned to death, for high treason!The condemnation was known and caused great emotion among the population. Immediately a petitioncovered itself with hundreds of signatures asking for the pardon of the condemned man. This act of courage by the populationdid not fail to impress the executioners. This time they did not dare go through with the sentence.And the death warrant was transformed into a sentence of life imprisonment.“The regime of terror that German ferocity has been reigning for nearly nine months over the unfortunateBelgium has just made a new victim in the person of a newspaper director in the province ofLuxemburg. This is Mr. Josen, a Belgian journalist of great merit and who had played, until the moment ofthe war, a big political role in this province.As soon as Belgium was occupied, Mr. Josen was put by the German military authorities on the listsuspects who had to be closely watched. But he was on his guard, because he knew that theleast pretext would be enough for the Germans to arrest him, accuse him of espionage and make him suffer the fate ofso many of his unfortunate compatriots who lost their lives under the Prussian bullets.Weeks and months passed. In vain the Germans waited for the opportunity to \"make theirbusiness\" to this courageous, but prudent and circumspect man, the occasion did not come. So they decided toproceed with one of those cowardly and infamous blows which they alone possess the mastery of.A month ago Mr. Josen intending to go to Holland went to Arlon and presented himself at the officeof the captain, head of the Kommandantur, to obtain a passport.The Hauptmann receives Mr. Josen very politely and, after examining his papers, declares himself ready for himissue the requested passport. But suddenly he gets up and says:Excuse me for a moment, I have an order to give outside, I\\'ll be right over to you.He leaves leaving Mr. Josen alone in his office. He leaves barely two minutes, comes back, settles in fronthis table and signs the visitor\\'s passport.But where is the stamp of the Kommandantur? he cries abruptly, and he begins to rummage inthe papers piled up in front of him.The stamp is not there! he howls! you stole it!And he throws himself on Mr. Josen, calls two gendarmes who run up. The prisoner is searched, holdingarms and naturally! - we find the stamp or rather one of the gendarmes \"removes\" it from one of theoutside pockets of the unfortunate Belgian journalist.This one may shout, protest, useless! He is arrested and taken, handcuffed, to prisonof Arlon. At the same time, the order is given to search Mr. Josen\\'s home. And there we discover- as only the Germans know how to discover a secret cipher; we also \"discover\" the draft of aencrypted telegram which is immediately decrypted using this key, and which contains military newsimportant, addressed to the commanders of the allied armies.That\\'s it! Mr. Josen, sent just days after his arrest before the councilof German war, is condemned to death, for high treason!The condemnation was known and caused great emotion among the population. Immediately a petitioncovered itself with hundreds of signatures asking for the pardon of the condemned man. This act of courage by the populationdid not fail to impress the executioners. This time they did not dare go through with the sentence.And the death warrant was transformed into a sentence of life imprisonment.Le Matin, which does not even know the exact name of its protege, proves once again by thisarticle that he no longer claims to be counted among the newspapers with which people like himmust can have a controversy. So we only point out the following to show in a wayconvincing the villainy of which this newspaper is guilty by denigrating the integrity of the judiciaryGerman :It is true that, on April 15, 1915, the Belgian journalist C. Joset, provincial councilor in Arlon, was condemnedto 3 years in prison for theft of an official stamp and to death for espionage, but, in this trial, the firstof these two offenses played only a wholly incidental role. The conviction was mainlymotivated by the factthe fact that Joset communicated to an enemy power secret information on theGerman troop movements; in full court and in a request for pardon addressed to hisExcellency the Governor General, Joset frankly confessed to having committed the crime of which weaccused him and he gave a detailed account of it. The court had to consider as an aggravating circumstance thefact that the culprit, possessing the special confidence of the German authorities and enjoying this head of advantagevery appreciable tages, has precisely abused this trust to make a secret trip to France. If thedeath sentence was nevertheless commuted to life imprisonment, Joset owes this favor only tohis sincere repentance and the signal services he has rendered to his fellow citizens since the beginning of the war.This being established, anyone who wishes to form an impartial opinion will judge as appropriate thevile slander which some detractors resort to in an attempt to tarnish the honor of officersand German officials.The General Government in Belgium',\n 'News publishedGovernments.Government.German general. .lies all attacks.The General Government in Belgium',\n 'Anyone who, without owning aexpress authorization from the competent authority,buys or tries to buy gold coins,silver or nickel or banknotesFrench at a price exceeding their face valuefinal, will be punished with a prison sentence.ment of up to one year and a fine of10,000 francs au maximum.The same penalties will be applied:1° to those who offer for sale or sellgold, silver or nickel coins orFrench banknotes to persons notduly authorized by the authority;
